--- Commit Message ---
LU-8585 llite: return parent fid as well for ll_encode_fh()

Lustre's native fhandle supports reporting the FID and parent FID.
While it supports both FIDs the parent FID was never set. Update
ll_encode_fh() to report the parent FID.

Change-Id: I286a7c1ee59a163f0df26bee675be72ecd53ab5e
Signed-off-by: James Simmons <jsimmons@infradead.org>

--- Message (wc-checkpatch, 2024-02-08 18:58:07.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18: Code-Review-1

--- Message (James Simmons, 2024-02-10 17:14:04.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18:

Neil this patch addresses a few shortcoming of parent FID handling.

Currently the fid handle for lustre supports both the file FID and parent FID but in reality the parent FID is never returned :-(

Second is we have an ioctl LL_IOC_GETPARENT that retrieves the parent FID. Well it doesn't return the true parent but the linkEA parent FID.
I believe the linkEA is for broken files under lost+found. So the linkno returns a specific linkEA parent. Currently if you call this ioctl for a normal file you don't get any parent FID since normally you don't have linkEAs for a file unless its broken.

This patch was attempting to use the fhandle API to do both above. That is why I was passing in the linkno into the fhandle. If that can't be done then we really can't remove the ioctl. I hope this makes it clear.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-02-10 18:58:38.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18:

> I believe the linkEA is for broken files under lost+found. So the
 > linkno returns a specific linkEA parent. Currently if you call this
 > ioctl for a normal file you don't get any parent FID since normally
 > you don't have linkEAs for a file unless its broken.
 
Al regular files should have a "link" xattr that is storing one or more reverse links for the parent directory FID and the filename in that directory. This is used for "lfs fid2path" in addition to LFSCK namespace repair so that a broken directory at the ldiskfs level can be repaired by hard-linking a file back into the directory.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2024-02-12 03:02:02.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18: Code-Review-1

> Patch Set 18:
> 
> Neil this patch addresses a few shortcoming of parent FID handling.
> 
> Currently the fid handle for lustre supports both the file FID and parent FID but in reality the parent FID is never returned :-(
> 
> Second is we have an ioctl LL_IOC_GETPARENT that retrieves the parent FID. Well it doesn't return the true parent but the linkEA parent FID.
> I believe the linkEA is for broken files under lost+found. So the linkno returns a specific linkEA parent. Currently if you call this ioctl for a normal file you don't get any parent FID since normally you don't have linkEAs for a file unless its broken.
> 
> This patch was attempting to use the fhandle API to do both above. That is why I was passing in the linkno into the fhandle. If that can't be done then we really can't remove the ioctl. I hope this makes it clear.

Thanks.  That makes is clear and is exactly the sort of description that I would expect in the commit message.

I think this functionality should remain as an ioctl.
Note that ext4 has 33 EXT4_IOC commands (Though some are 32 bit compat versions).
XFS has about 50
vtrfs has about 78

It is perfectly OK to have ioctl commands for fs-specific functionality.  It is appropriate to review them to ensure that they cannot be implemented in some more "standard" way, but if that review suggests there is no alternative, we can accept that and not expect it to be a problem upstream.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-03-01 03:07:15.000000000) ---
Patch Set 22: Code-Review-1

(5 comments)

This shouldn't introduce a new failure case if the parent cannot be found.  That wasn't an error before, and shouldn't be an error now.

In some regards, this is abusing the name_to_handle_at() interface and (it seems like) adding unnecessary overhead.  Internally that function is asking for a file handle *without* the parent, but ll_encode_fh() is now ignoring the wishes of the caller and always adding the parent:

        /* we ask for a non connectable maybe decodeable file handle */
        retval = exportfs_encode_fh(path->dentry,
                                    (struct fid *)handle->f_handle,
                                    &handle_dwords, fh_flags);

--- Message (James Simmons, 2024-03-02 23:41:03.000000000) ---
Patch Set 22:

Neil is this okay?

--- Message (James Simmons, 2024-03-04 16:50:11.000000000) ---
Patch Set 22:

Looking at the newer kernels it appears parent is never set so the kernel code to get parent FIDs are noops. Don't know if this approach is okay then. Waiting from Neil to see if its the case. Still would be great if we could get the parent FID some how. If we can't do it this way we can update the ioctl then to get the true parent when linkno = -1.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2024-03-04 21:59:12.000000000) ---
Patch Set 22: Code-Review-1

I don't think this is a good idea.
This means that when a file is moved from one directory to another the handle will change.  That will confuse code that reasonably expects it not to.

The only reason we have the "parent" thing at all is for the "subtree_check" nfsd export option which I was never quite brave enough the deprecate.
As you note, it isn't accessible from name_to_handle_at() and is discouraged from nfsd.

I really think that if you want a way to get the parent FID, that should be a lustre-specific ioctl.  Don't try to overload the handle code - it isn't a good fit.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-03-04 23:43:09.000000000) ---
Patch Set 22:

> update the ioctl then to get the true parent when linkno = -1

What does "true parent" even mean for a file with multiple hard links?  

Is the goal of this patch just to get rid of the ioctl() or what is deficient with the current llapi_fd2parent() call?  There were patches https://review.whamcloud.com/35648 and https://review.whamcloud.com/33209 that added a new ioctl(LL_IOC_FID2PARENT) call, if that is what you are looking for?

--- Message (James Simmons, 2024-03-04 23:49:03.000000000) ---
Patch Set 22:

The problem is all the llapi_*2parent() function normally never return a parent. It would be nice to return a parent even if no hard links exist for the file.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-03-04 23:58:44.000000000) ---
Patch Set 22:

> The problem is all the llapi_*2parent() function normally never
 > return a parent. It would be nice to return a parent even if no
 > hard links exist for the file.

I'm not sure what you mean?  llapi_fid2path() *has* to find a parent FID for it to work, so if llapi_fd2parent() is not returning a parent then something is wrong.  Getting the parent from the dcache isn't guaranteed, but getting it from the "link" xattr (as it does today) should work?

 # lfs path2fid --parents /myth/tmp/links/hosts
 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/hosts [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link1
 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link2 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link3
 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link4 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link5
 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link6 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link7
 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link8 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link9
 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link11 [0x200016b84:0x10a9a:0x0]/link12
 :

This ioctl() is currently restricted to root (or other capable process), or allowed globally if "user_fid2path" is enabled on the client mountpoint:

        if (!capable(CAP_DAC_READ_SEARCH) &&
            !test_bit(LL_SBI_USER_FID2PATH, ll_i2sbi(inode)->ll_flags))
                RETURN(-EPERM);

That could probably be relaxed to return parents owned by the current user or something?
